The Sun's Hidden Influence on Heat and Cold
This passage presents the third proof: the sun's rays overpower other stars, but their influence remains, affecting temperature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the sun's conjunction with other planets influences temperature on Earth, even when those planets are hidden by sunlight.

Core Idea
The sun's rays hide stars, but their power still affects weather.

This passage presents the third proof of the sun's wisdom. The author points to a subtle but observable phenomenon: summer days differ in heat because of the sun's alignment with other planets. The lesson shows that visible dominance does not erase hidden influences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once for rhythm, then the English translation. Note the author's claim about hidden planetary power.
2
Understand the paradox
The sun's light hides other stars, but the author insists their power persists. Why is this important? Reflect on how things can be unseen yet effective.
3
Connect the example to the explanation
The example of varying summer heat is explained by the sun's conjunction (alignment) with hot or cold planets. Trace how the author reasons from observation to cause.
4
Reflect on the broader wisdom
Consider the cosmic interconnectedness: all celestial bodies contribute to earthly conditions. This points to design and purpose beyond mere appearance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الثالث : أن الشمس إذا ظهرت ، اختفت بكمال شعاعها سائر الكواكب ، إلا أنها وإن خفيت ، إلا أن قوتها باقية. ولذلك فإنه يكون يوم من الصيف ، أحر من يوم آخر . وما ذاك إلا بسبب أن الشمس إذا قارنت في سيرها كوكباً حاراً ، فإنه يزداد حر الهواء ، وبالضد منه في جانب البرد .
And the third aspect: That when the sun appears, all the other planets disappear by its complete rays. However, even though they are hidden, their power remains. Because of this, one day of summer is hotter than another day. That is only because when the sun in its course is in conjunction with a hot planet, then the heat of the air increases, and conversely on the side of cold.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is the third proof (الوجه الثالث) of the sun's wisdom. It addresses the sun's overpowering light: when the sun rises, its rays hide all other stars. But this does not mean those stars lose their influence; their power persists. The author gives a tangible example: summer days vary in heat. The reason is that the sun's conjunction with a hot planet (like Mars or Venus) intensifies the air's heat, while conjunction with a cold planet produces the opposite. Thus, even though the stars are invisible, their effects are real and measurable. This demonstrates that the cosmos is finely tuned such that each celestial body contributes to earthly conditions, and the sun's role is central but not exclusive. The wisdom lies in this hidden but real interaction.

Key Terms
الشمس
الشعاع
الكواكب
القوة
الحر
البرد
المقارنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Stars have no influence when hidden by sunlight.
Correction: The author shows that their power remains, affecting temperature even when invisible.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say one summer day can be hotter than another?
A) Because the sun moves closer to the earth.
B) Because the moon's phases change.
C) Because the sun is in conjunction with a hot planet.
D) Because of wind patterns on earth.

Key Takeaway
The sun's conjunction with other planets influences temperature on Earth, even when those planets are invisible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The hidden planets still affect the temperature even when you cannot see them. What hidden sin or bad habit is affecting your spiritual 'climate' right now, and are you willing to expose it to the light of repentance today?
?
The author shows that a small change (conjunction) can make a big difference. Think about one minor adjustment in your daily routine—like a short dhikr or avoiding a glance—that could shift your entire day toward Allah. Will you commit to it starting tomorrow?
?
When the sun is with a hot planet, the heat increases. Who are the people you spend most of your time with? Are they raising your spiritual temperature (imān) or cooling it? What will you do about it this week?

Animals Appear Dead at Night and Revive at Dawn
Fourth proof using daily revival of animals at dawn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth proof from Al-Matalib al-Aliyah that uses the daily revival of animals at dawn as a sign of the sun's wisdom and divine power.

Core Idea
The sun's daily renewal of life in animals mirrors divine resurrection.

This passage presents the fourth proof for the wisdom in the sun's creation. The author observes that all animals appear lifeless at night, but with the dawn's light, vitality returns. This phenomenon serves as a striking analogy for the power of God over life and death.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation together. Note the structure: statement of observation, result, and an incomplete comparison.
The text is cut off at 'مجرى' – think about how it might conclude.
2
Identify the proof's logic
The proof draws an analogy between animals at night (like dead) and animals at dawn (revived). Recognize the sun's light as the agent of revival.
3
Reflect on the deeper meaning
Consider that the author likely intends this as a sign of resurrection or divine power. How does this daily observation point to God's wisdom?
This connects the physical phenomenon to theological truth.
4
Ponder the incomplete part
The text ends with 'فيجري هذا، مجرى' (this runs, like the course of). Speculate what comparison might follow, e.g., 'like the resurrection of the dead'.
This encourages engagement with the text's intended meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الرابع : إنا نرى جميع الحيوانات في الليل ، كالميتة . فإذا طلع نور الصبح ظهرت في أجساد الحيوانات ، نور الحياة ، فيجري هذا ، مجرى
And the fourth aspect: That we see all animals at night as if dead. Then when the light of dawn rises, the light of life appears in the bodies of animals. This runs, like the course of
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is the fourth proof (الوجه الرابع) of the sun's wisdom. It draws an analogy between animals at night and death. At night, animals appear lifeless, but with the appearance of the sun's morning light, vitality returns. The text is cut off, but it clearly intends to show that the sun's light is a source of life and animation. The incomplete phrase 'فيجري هذا، مجرى' suggests a comparison, likely to the resurrection or to the spiritual life. The proof highlights the sun's role in daily renewal and its parallel to divine power over life and death.

Key Terms

نور الصبح
نور الحياة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The passage is purely biological and has no theological significance.
Correction: In context, this proof is a sign of God's wisdom in creating the sun as a source of life and a daily reminder of resurrection.

Checkpoint
According to the fourth proof, what happens to animals when the light of dawn rises?
A) They continue sleeping.
B) The light of life appears in their bodies.
C) They become dead.
D) They hide from the sun.

Key Takeaway
The daily revival of animals at dawn is a powerful sign of the sun's life-giving role and a reminder of God's power over death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
At night, animals are 'as if dead,' but at dawn they are full of life. In your own spiritual life, are there areas where you feel 'as if alive' but lack true vitality? What 'dawn' does God need to shine on you today? What one concrete step will you take this week to expose yourself to that light?
?
The proof shows that the sun's light brings life to animals. What is the 'sun' that brings life to your soul? Have you been hiding from it? Where will you intentionally place yourself under its rays starting tomorrow morning?
?
The passage uses the word 'كالميتة' (like dead) to describe animals at night. Are there parts of your faith that are only 'like' real but lack substance? What will you do to move from resemblance to reality before the true dawn arrives?
